class _NeuralGridDecoderEmbedding(nn.Module):
    """Parallel decoder head for a fixed-size neural token grid (output modalities).

    Mirrors ``ImageTokenDecoderEmbedding``'s ``forward_embed`` / ``forward_logits``
    contract so 4M routes these through its **parallel** decoder branch: target ids are
    embedded (``d['x']``), per-cell positional + modality embeddings are added
    (``d['emb']``), and ``forward_logits`` projects decoder outputs to vocab logits.
    The decoder replaces ``d['x']`` with its mask token, so the model must *predict*
    each target — there is no leakage. Subclasses define the positional layout.

    Subclasses set ``self.vocab_size`` / ``self.n_positions`` / ``self.dim_tokens`` in
    ``__init__`` then call ``self.init(dim_tokens)`` (4M calls it lazily otherwise).
    """

    def init(self, dim_tokens: int = 768, init_std: float = 0.02) -> None:
        self.dim_tokens = dim_tokens
        # No padding_idx: code 0 is a real token; absence is handled by presence masking.
        self.token_emb = nn.Embedding(self.vocab_size, dim_tokens)
        self.to_logits = nn.Linear(dim_tokens, self.vocab_size, bias=False)
        self.mod_emb = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(1, 1, dim_tokens))
        nn.init.normal_(self.mod_emb, std=init_std)
        self._build_positions(dim_tokens, init_std)

    def _build_positions(self, dim_tokens: int, init_std: float) -> None:
        raise NotImplementedError

    def _position_embedding(self) -> torch.Tensor:
        """Fixed per-cell positional embedding of shape ``(n_positions, D)``."""
        raise NotImplementedError

    def forward_embed(self, d: Dict[str, torch.Tensor]) -> Dict[str, torch.Tensor]:
        assert self.dim_tokens is not None, "Call init(dim_tokens) before forward_embed."
        ids = d["tensor"]
        B = ids.shape[0]
        ids = ids.reshape(B, -1)
        x = self.token_emb(ids)
        x_emb = repeat(
            self._position_embedding().unsqueeze(0) + self.mod_emb, "() n d -> b n d", b=B
        )
        d["x"] = x
        d["emb"] = x_emb
        d["ids"] = ids
        return d

    def forward_logits(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        return self.to_logits(x)

    @torch.jit.ignore
    def no_weight_decay(self):
        return set()


class MegRVQDecoderEmbedding(_NeuralGridDecoderEmbedding):
    """One MEG RVQ-layer head: ``(B, 128)`` ids of a 16x8 grid, vocab 512.

    Positions mirror ``MegEncoderEmbedding``: a **learned** embedding for the 16
    unordered latent sources and **sincos** for the 8 ordered time steps, summed
    per cell. Four of these (one per RVQ layer) reconstruct a MEG token in parallel.
    """

    def __init__(
        self,
        vocab_size: int = MEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
        n_sources: int = MEG_N_SOURCES,
        n_time: int = MEG_N_TIME,
        dim_tokens: int | None = None,
        **kwargs,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        self.vocab_size = vocab_size
        self.n_sources = n_sources
        self.n_time = n_time
        self.n_positions = n_sources * n_time
        self.dim_tokens = dim_tokens
        if dim_tokens is not None:
            self.init(dim_tokens)

    def _build_positions(self, dim_tokens: int, init_std: float) -> None:
        self.source_emb = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(self.n_sources, dim_tokens))
        nn.init.normal_(self.source_emb, std=init_std)
        time_emb = build_1d_sincos_posemb(max_len=self.n_time, embed_dim=dim_tokens)[0]
        self.register_buffer("time_emb", time_emb)  # (n_time, D)
        cells = torch.arange(self.n_positions)
        self.register_buffer("src_idx", cells // self.n_time)
        self.register_buffer("time_idx", cells % self.n_time)

    def _position_embedding(self) -> torch.Tensor:
        return self.source_emb[self.src_idx] + self.time_emb[self.time_idx]

    @torch.jit.ignore
    def no_weight_decay(self):
        return {"source_emb"}


class EegDecoderEmbedding(_NeuralGridDecoderEmbedding):
    """EEG head: ``(B, 17)`` ids of a 1D sequence, vocab 8192, sincos positions."""

    def __init__(
        self,
        vocab_size: int = EEG_VOCAB_SIZE,
        max_length: int = EEG_TOKENS_PER_TRIAL,
        dim_tokens: int | None = None,
        sincos_pos_emb: bool = True,
        **kwargs,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        self.vocab_size = vocab_size
        self.n_positions = max_length
        self.sincos_pos_emb = sincos_pos_emb
        self.dim_tokens = dim_tokens
        if dim_tokens is not None:
            self.init(dim_tokens)

    def _build_positions(self, dim_tokens: int, init_std: float) -> None:
        if self.sincos_pos_emb:
            pos = build_1d_sincos_posemb(max_len=self.n_positions, embed_dim=dim_tokens)[0]
            self.register_buffer("pos_emb", pos)  # (n_positions, D)
        else:
            self.pos_emb = nn.Parameter(torch.zeros(self.n_positions, dim_tokens))
            nn.init.normal_(self.pos_emb, std=init_std)

    def _position_embedding(self) -> torch.Tensor:
        return self.pos_emb

class NeuralTargetTransform(AbstractTransform):
    """Passthrough for neural OUTPUT modalities (tok_meg_rvq*, tok_eeg_out).

    The trial pick + RVQ-layer extraction happen once per sample in the dataloader
    rename seam (so the 4 MEG heads stay coherent), so by the time this runs the value
    is already a single-trial 1-D code array. We only clip to the head's vocab and cast
    to int64. See ``neural_trial_transform.NeuralTargetSplitter``.
    """

    def __init__(self, code_max: int):
        self.code_max = code_max

    def load(self, path: str) -> np.ndarray:
        return np.load(path, allow_pickle=False)

    def preprocess(self, sample: np.ndarray) -> torch.Tensor:
        tokens = np.clip(np.asarray(sample), 0, self.code_max)
        return torch.from_numpy(tokens).long()

    def image_augment(self, v, *args, **kwargs):
        return v

    def postprocess(self, sample):
        return sample

def extract_presence_flags(mod_dict: dict) -> dict[str, bool]:
    """Pop ``meg_mask`` / ``eeg_mask`` from ``mod_dict`` and return presence map."""
    presence: dict[str, bool] = {}
    for tok_mod, flag_mod in PRESENCE_FLAGS.items():

            presence[tok_mod] = True
            continue
        presence[tok_mod] = _read_presence_flag(mod_dict.pop(flag_mod))
    return presence
+
def extract_presence_flags(mod_dict: dict) -> dict[str, bool]:
    """Pop ``meg_mask`` / ``eeg_mask`` from ``mod_dict`` and return presence map.

    Several token modalities may share one flag (e.g. the four ``tok_meg_rvq*`` heads
    all gate on ``meg_mask``), so read every flag before removing the unique flag keys.
    """
    presence: dict[str, bool] = {}
    for tok_mod, flag_mod in PRESENCE_FLAGS.items():
        presence[tok_mod] = (
            _read_presence_flag(mod_dict[flag_mod]) if flag_mod in mod_dict else True
        )
    for flag_mod in set(PRESENCE_FLAGS.values()):
        mod_dict.pop(flag_mod, None)
    return presence

class EegTrialSampleTransform(NeuralTrialSampleTransform):
    """EEG trial sampler: ``(n_trials, 17)`` -> ``(17,)`` (flat 1D sequence)."""

    def __init__(self, training: bool = True, seed: int | None = None):

class NeuralTargetSplitter:
    """Materialize neural OUTPUT heads from one shared trial, in-place on a sample dict.

    The dataloader's ``rename_modalities`` step fans the on-disk ``tok_meg`` / ``tok_eeg``
    folder out to every output modality that reads it, so all four ``tok_meg_rvq*`` keys
    initially **alias the same** ``(n_trials, 16, 8, 4)`` array. This splitter picks **one**
    trial for that array and slices it into the four per-RVQ-layer ``(128,)`` targets — so
    the four MEG heads always describe the *same* MEG token. EEG (single codebook) is a
    single ``(17,)`` head. Absent (sentinel) data becomes the placeholder code; presence
    masking then zeroes its loss. See ``notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md`` §6.

    One pick per source per call ⇒ coherent across heads; the picked trial is exactly what
    the loss scores, because that single array is both embedded and used as the target ids.
    """

    def __init__(self, training: bool = True, seed: int | None = None):
        self._meg = MegTrialSampleTransform(training=training, seed=seed)
        self._eeg = EegTrialSampleTransform(training=training, seed=seed)

    def __call__(self, sample: dict) -> dict:
        meg_mods = [m for m in MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES if m in sample]
        if meg_mods:
            grid, _valid = self._meg(sample[meg_mods[0]])  # (128, n_rvq); one shared pick
            for q, mod in enumerate(MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES):
                if mod in sample:
                    sample[mod] = np.ascontiguousarray(grid[:, q])
        if EEG_OUT_MODALITY in sample:
            tokens, _valid = self._eeg(sample[EEG_OUT_MODALITY])  # (17,)
            sample[EEG_OUT_MODALITY] = tokens
        return sample

def _set_neural_target_splitter(training: bool) -> None:
    """Install the per-sample neural-output trial splitter (train vs eval sampling)."""

    from neural_trial_transform import NeuralTargetSplitter

    _NEURAL_SPLITTER = NeuralTargetSplitter(training=training)


def _rename_modalities(sample, modality_paths):
    """Stock rename assumes every path exists; THINGS omits optional ``crop_settings`` tars.

    Also the single point where neural OUTPUT heads are materialized: rename fans the
    ``tok_meg`` / ``tok_eeg`` folder out to the output modalities (aliasing one array),
    then the splitter picks one trial and slices the per-head targets — so the 4 MEG RVQ
    heads stay coherent. No-op when no neural output modality is requested.
    """
    present = {out: src for out, src in modality_paths.items() if src in sample}
    if not present:
        return sample
    renamed = _ORIG_RENAME_MODALITIES(sample, present)
    if _NEURAL_SPLITTER is not None:
        _NEURAL_SPLITTER(renamed)
    return renamed

📝 Write 4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml
/Users/Siddharth/neural-foundation-model/4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml
# Smoke data variant: NEURAL AS OUTPUT (reconstruction regularizer).
#
# Predict vision + MEG + EEG tokens from vision alone. Neural is in out_domains only
# (not in_domains), so there is nothing to copy — the heads must reconstruct the brain
# tokens from the RGB/depth representation, which regularizes the shared encoder/decoder.
#
# MEG uses 4 parallel heads, one per RVQ layer (tok_meg_rvq0..3, vocab 512, 16x8 grid);
# EEG uses one head (tok_eeg_out, vocab 8192, 17 tokens). All read the existing tok_meg /
# tok_eeg folders (no repack). The dataloader picks ONE trial per sample and splits it so
# the 4 MEG heads stay coherent. See notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md §6.
#
# These output heads are deliberately kept OUT of the validation tasks
# (configs/4m_things_val_tasks.yaml) — they exist purely to shape upstream weights.
train:
  datasets:
    things:
      type: multimodal
      use_wds: true
      # tok_meg / tok_eeg folders are loaded once; the output heads fan out from them.
      data_path: /project/data/train/things/[tok_rgb,tok_depth,tok_meg,tok_eeg,meg_mask,eeg_mask]/shard_{000..000}.tar
      in_domains: tok_rgb-tok_depth                 # vision only on the encoder
      out_domains: tok_rgb-tok_depth-tok_meg_rvq0-tok_meg_rvq1-tok_meg_rvq2-tok_meg_rvq3-tok_eeg_out
      main_augment_domain: tok_rgb
      tok_train_aug: false
      input_alphas: "1.0-1.0"                       # rgb, depth
      target_alphas: "1.0"                          # uniform across all 7 targets
      aligned_captions: false
      wds_n_repeats: 1
      wds_shuffle_buffer_tar: 50
      wds_shuffle_buffer_repeat: 50
  weights: [1.0]

    def test_neural_heads_overfit_one_batch(self):
        """The strongest wiring check: each neural head drives its loss down on one batch."""
        from fourm_dataloader import patch_pretrain_utils

        patch_pretrain_utils()
        model, batch, neural = self._batch_and_model()
        model.train()
        opt = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=2e-3, betas=(0.9, 0.95))
        n_targets = sum(int((~batch[m]["target_mask"]).sum()) for m in batch)

        def step():
            opt.zero_grad()
            loss, mod_loss = model(
                batch, num_encoder_tokens=256, num_decoder_tokens=n_targets + 256,
                loss_type="mod",
            )
            loss.backward()
            opt.step()
            return {m: float(mod_loss[m].detach()) for m in neural}

        first = step()
        for _ in range(60):
            last = step()
        for m in neural:
            assert last[m] < first[m] - 0.5, f"{m}: {first[m]:.3f} -> {last[m]:.3f} (not learning)"

Tool reply2026-05-27T20:47:47.041Z
1	"""End-to-end 4M data pipeline integration tests on synthetic shards.
2	
3	Exercises the full 4M WebDataset chain that
4	``build_wds_fm_pretraining_dataloader`` runs on real training data, except
5	we substitute synthetic tars and stop before the masking / Dirichlet step
6	(which requires a text tokenizer we don't need for storage-format validation).
7	
8	The pipeline under test:
9	    ResampledShards
10	    -> multi_tarfile_samples       (zips tars by __key__)
11	    -> wds.shuffle                  (intra-shard shuffle)
12	    -> wds.decode(wds_decoder)      (npy -> ndarray)
13	    -> remove_extensions            (strip ".npy")
14	    -> filter_metadata              (drop __key__ / __url__)
15	    -> tok_to_int64                 (tok_* npy int16 -> int64)
16	    -> rename_modalities            (folder name -> modality name)
17	
18	These are the same primitives 4M chains internally; we just stop before
19	``UnifiedMasking``. The point of this test layer is to prove the
20	Option 1 storage layout traverses the entire 4M decode path cleanly.
21	"""
22	
23	from __future__ import annotations
24	
25	import io
26	import sys
27	import tarfile
28	from functools import partial
29	from pathlib import Path
30	from typing import Iterable
31	
32	import numpy as np
33	import pytest
34	import webdataset as wds
35	
36	from neural_constants import MEG_GRID_SHAPE, MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE, TOK_RGB_TOKENS_PER_IMAGE
37	
38	from fourm.data.unified_datasets import (
39	    filter_metadata,
40	    multi_tarfile_samples,
41	    remove_extensions,
42	    rename_modalities,
43	    tok_to_int64,
44	    wds_decoder,
45	)
46	# fourm's local map shadows builtin; expose as keyless_map for clarity.
47	from fourm.data.unified_datasets import map as keyless_map  # noqa: E402
48	
49	sys.path.insert(0, str(Path(__file__).resolve().parent))
50	from neural_trial_transform import (  # noqa: E402
51	    MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE,
52	    MegTrialSampleTransform,
53	    is_placeholder,
54	)
55	
56	
57	# ---------- shard fixture helpers ----------------------------------------
58	
59	
60	def _make_tar(path: Path, entries: Iterable[tuple[str, str, bytes]]) -> None:
61	    path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
62	    with tarfile.open(path, "w") as tar:
63	        for key, ext, data in entries:
64	            info = tarfile.TarInfo(name=f"{key}.{ext}")
65	            info.size = len(data)
66	            tar.addfile(info, io.BytesIO(data))
67	
68	
69	def _npy_bytes(arr: np.ndarray) -> bytes:
70	    buf = io.BytesIO()
71	    np.save(buf, arr, allow_pickle=False)
72	    return buf.getvalue()
73	
74	
75	def _synthesize_three_shards(root: Path, n_per_shard: int = 20) -> list[str]:
76	    """Write 3 shards with n_per_shard image ids each.
77	
78	    Modalities written:
79	      tok_rgb, tok_depth, tok_meg, meg_mask, crop_settings
80	
81	    Note: ``meg_mask`` deliberately does NOT start with ``tok_`` because 4M's
82	    ``tok_to_int64`` filter casts any ``tok_*`` value to int64 — which would
83	    silently convert our uint8 presence flag.
84	
85	    Half the MEG entries (alternating ids) are sentinel placeholders.
86	    """
87	    all_ids: list[str] = []
88	    for shard_idx in range(3):
89	        ids = [
90	            f"{shard_idx * n_per_shard + j + 1:09d}" for j in range(n_per_shard)
91	        ]
92	        all_ids.extend(ids)
93	
94	        # Dense tokenized vision modalities.
95	        _make_tar(
96	            root / f"tok_rgb/shard_{shard_idx:03d}.tar",
97	            [
98	                (
99	                    image_id,
100	                    "npy",
101	                    _npy_bytes(
102	                        np.full((TOK_RGB_TOKENS_PER_IMAGE,), int(image_id) % 100, dtype=np.int16)
103	                    ),
104	                )
105	                for image_id in ids
106	            ],
107	        )
108	        _make_tar(
109	            root / f"tok_depth/shard_{shard_idx:03d}.tar",
110	            [
111	                (image_id, "npy", _npy_bytes(np.zeros((TOK_RGB_TOKENS_PER_IMAGE,), dtype=np.int16)))
112	                for image_id in ids
113	            ],
114	        )
115	
116	        # MEG: alternate real / placeholder.
117	        meg_entries: list[tuple[str, str, bytes]] = []
118	        mask_entries: list[tuple[str, str, bytes]] = []
119	        for j, image_id in enumerate(ids):
120	            if j % 2 == 0:
121	                # Real: variable trial count.
122	                n_trials = 1 + (j % 4)
123	                arr = np.full(
124	                    (n_trials, *MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE),
125	                    int(image_id) % 256,
126	                    dtype=np.int16,
127	                )
128	                meg_entries.append((image_id, "npy", _npy_bytes(arr)))
129	                mask_entries.append(
130	                    (image_id, "npy", _npy_bytes(np.array([1], dtype=np.uint8)))
131	                )
132	            else:
133	                meg_entries.append(
134	                    (
135	                        image_id,
136	                        "npy",
137	                        _npy_bytes(np.full((1, *MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE), -1, dtype=np.int16)),
138	                    )
139	                )
140	                mask_entries.append(
141	                    (image_id, "npy", _npy_bytes(np.array([0], dtype=np.uint8)))
142	                )
143	        _make_tar(root / f"tok_meg/shard_{shard_idx:03d}.tar", meg_entries)
144	        _make_tar(root / f"meg_mask/shard_{shard_idx:03d}.tar", mask_entries)
145	
146	        # Crop settings: not used here but typically required by 4M for tok_*.
147	        _make_tar(
148	            root / f"crop_settings/shard_{shard_idx:03d}.tar",
149	            [
150	                (
151	                    image_id,
152	                    "npy",
153	                    _npy_bytes(np.zeros((1, 5), dtype=np.float32)),
154	                )
155	                for image_id in ids
156	            ],
157	        )
158	    return all_ids

    def test_neural_output_heads_materialized_and_coherent(self, shard_root: Path):
        """Real pipeline: rename fan-out + splitter produce coherent per-head targets.

        Each MEG trial is a distinct constant, so we can assert all four RVQ heads land
        on the *same* trial (coherence) and have the right flat shapes/dtypes.
        """
        import fourm_neural_modalities  # noqa: F401  (registers output modalities)
        from fourm.data import unified_datasets as ud
        from fourm_dataloader import (
            _extend_modality_paths,
            patch_pretrain_utils,
            unpatch_pretrain_utils,
        )
        from neural_constants import (
            EEG_OUT_MODALITY,
            EEG_TOKENS_PER_TRIAL,
            EEG_TRIAL_SHAPE,
            MEG_POSITIONS_PER_TRIAL,
            MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES,
        )
        from train_4m import _build_modality_info

        root = shard_root
        ids = ["000000001", "000000002"]
        n_trials = 5
        for mod_dir, entries in (
            ("tok_rgb", [(i, _npy_bytes(np.full((TOK_RGB_TOKENS_PER_IMAGE,), 1, np.int16))) for i in ids]),
            # MEG trial t is the constant (t+1) everywhere -> identifies the picked trial.
            ("tok_meg", [(i, _npy_bytes(np.stack([np.full(MEG_TRIAL_SHAPE, t + 1, np.int16) for t in range(n_trials)]))) for i in ids]),
            ("tok_eeg", [(i, _npy_bytes(np.stack([np.full(EEG_TRIAL_SHAPE, t + 1, np.int16) for t in range(n_trials)]))) for i in ids]),
            ("meg_mask", [(i, _npy_bytes(np.array([1], np.uint8))) for i in ids]),
            ("eeg_mask", [(i, _npy_bytes(np.array([1], np.uint8))) for i in ids]),
        ):
            _make_tar(root / f"{mod_dir}/shard_000.tar", [(k, "npy", b) for k, b in entries])

        out_domains = ["tok_rgb", *MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES, EEG_OUT_MODALITY]
        mod_info = _build_modality_info(out_domains)
        paths = _extend_modality_paths(mod_info)

        patch_pretrain_utils()  # installs _rename_modalities + train-mode splitter
        try:
            pipeline = wds.DataPipeline(
                wds.SimpleShardList(
                    f"{root}/[tok_rgb,tok_meg,tok_eeg,meg_mask,eeg_mask]/shard_{{000..000}}.tar"
                ),
                partial(multi_tarfile_samples, handler=_fail_handler),
                wds.decode(wds_decoder),
                wds.map(remove_extensions),
                keyless_map(filter_metadata),
                keyless_map(tok_to_int64),
                keyless_map(partial(ud.rename_modalities, modality_paths=paths)),
            )
            n = 0
            for sample in pipeline:
                n += 1
                for mod in MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES:
                    assert sample[mod].shape == (MEG_POSITIONS_PER_TRIAL,), mod
                assert sample[EEG_OUT_MODALITY].shape == (EEG_TOKENS_PER_TRIAL,)
                # All four MEG heads must come from one trial -> one shared constant.
                picked = {int(np.unique(sample[mod])[0]) for mod in MEG_RVQ_OUT_MODALITIES}
                assert len(picked) == 1, f"RVQ heads decohered across trials: {picked}"
        finally:
            unpatch_pretrain_utils()
        assert n == 2

        self, shard_root: Path
    ):

## 6. If neural ever becomes a target (future)

You'd then confront the parallel-vs-autoregressive decoder choice (see §2). The
right move would be a **parallel** decoder over the `16×8` grid with **4 logit heads**
(one per RVQ layer) — *not* `seq_token`'s autoregressive path. Out of scope while
neural is input-only.

---

Related: [[neural_fm_modal_main_collision]] (Modal entrypoint gotcha).
+
## 6. Neural as a target (implemented): a reconstruction regularizer

Predicting MEG/EEG from vision shapes the shared encoder/decoder without touching the
validation tasks. This is **additive**: the input-only `tok_meg` / `tok_eeg` modalities
are unchanged; new *output* modalities are registered alongside them.

### The four design forces (and how each is resolved)

| Force | Resolution |
|---|---|
| `seq_token` targets hit 4M's **autoregressive** decoder path (`fm.cat_decoder_tensors`, the left-shift `logical_or` that drops scattered `image_mask` targets — the "MEG loss = 0" bug) | give the output mods a **custom `type: neural_grid`**, which falls through to the **parallel** decoder branch |
| `type: img` would route correctly **but** the trainer overwrites img `max_tokens` with `(image_size/patch_size)²` (`run_training_4m.setup_modality_info`) — always a square; our grids are **128** and **17** | `neural_grid` is **not** `img`, so the square rule skips it and our `max_tokens` survives |
| 4M's loss is **one cross-entropy head per modality**; MEG has 4 layer-specific RVQ codebooks | **4 output modalities** `tok_meg_rvq0..3` (vocab 512, 16×8 grid), one head each; loss sums across them. EEG is one head `tok_eeg_out` (vocab 8192, 17) |
| Targets must come from real on-disk data without a repack | each head reads an existing folder via `path` (`tok_meg` / `tok_eeg`); 4M's `rename_modalities` fans one folder out to several modalities |

So MEG decodes as a **parallel `16×8` grid with 4 logit heads** — exactly the §2 prescription,
realized without editing `external/ml-4m/`. The decoder embeddings
(`MegRVQDecoderEmbedding`, `EegDecoderEmbedding`) mirror the encoder's positional logic:
axial (learned-source ⊕ sincos-time) for MEG, sincos-1D for EEG.

### Trial sampling ↔ loss-target coherence (the subtle part)

A tokenized neural example has many trials on disk; we sample **one** per step. Two
coherence guarantees matter, and both are structural — not left to chance:

1. **Within a head, the embedded tokens and the loss target are the same array.** The
   trial is sampled **once**, in the data loader (CPU), producing a single tensor `T`.
   The decoder embedding's `forward_embed` sets `d['ids'] = d['tensor'] (= T)`;
   `cat_decoder_tensors` uses `d['ids']` as the target and *replaces* the decoder input
   with the mask token. So the label is exactly the sampled trial, the model never sees
   it as input (no leakage), and there is no second sampling between forward and backprop.

2. **Across the 4 MEG heads, all layers come from the same trial.** If each head ran its
   own sampling transform it could pick a *different* trial → the 4 RVQ codes would
   describe different MEG tokens. Instead `NeuralTargetSplitter` (invoked once per sample
   in the `rename_modalities` seam) picks **one** trial and slices all four layers from it.

### Leakage / config guidance

Because MEG's input (summed grid `tok_meg`) and outputs (`tok_meg_rvq*`) are *different*
modality names, putting both in one config lets the encoder see cells the decoder also
predicts → trivial copying, weak gradient. The shipped regularizer config
(`configs/4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml`) avoids this by predicting neural **from
vision** (`in: rgb+depth → out: rgb+depth+meg_rvq*+eeg_out`); neural is never an encoder
input. EEG-as-both is leak-free (single modality split by `image_mask`), MEG-as-both is not.

---

Related: [[neural_fm_modal_main_collision]] (Modal entrypoint gotcha).

| Modality | On-disk | After trial pick | Role | Vocab constant |
|----------|---------|------------------|------|----------------|
| `tok_meg` | `(n_trials, 16, 8, 4)` | `(128, 4)` = `(16·8 cells, 4 RVQ)` | input-only | `MEG_VOCAB_SIZE` (per layer) |
| `tok_eeg` | `(n_trials, 17)` | `(17,)` | input-only | `EEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_meg_rvq0..3` | reads `tok_meg` folder | `(128,)` each (one RVQ layer) | **output** (4 heads) | `MEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_eeg_out` | reads `tok_eeg` folder | `(17,)` | **output** (1 head) | `EEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_rgb` | `(196,)` int16 | `(196,)` | input + target | `TOK_RGB_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_depth` | `(196,)` int16 | `(196,)` | input + target | `TOK_DEPTH_VOCAB_SIZE` |

As **inputs**, MEG keeps its `16×8` grid and the 4 RVQ layers are summed inside
`MegEncoderEmbedding`; `tok_meg` / `tok_eeg` are encoded but never predicted. As
**outputs** (a reconstruction regularizer), MEG is predicted by 4 parallel heads — one
per RVQ layer (`tok_meg_rvq0..3`, `type: neural_grid`) — and EEG by one head
(`tok_eeg_out`). The output heads read the same on-disk folders (no repack); the loader
picks one trial per sample and splits it so the 4 MEG heads stay coherent. They are kept
**out of the validation tasks** on purpose. Why each axis/role is treated this way, plus
the trial↔loss coherence guarantee: [`notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md`](../notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md) §6.

`MegEncoderEmbedding` (not flattened). MEG/EEG are **input-only** — encoded but never
predicted. Why each axis is treated this way: [`notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md`](../notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md).
+
| `tok_meg` | `(n_trials, 16, 8, 4)` | `(128, 4)` = `(16·8 cells, 4 RVQ)` | input-only | `MEG_VOCAB_SIZE` (per layer) |
| `tok_eeg` | `(n_trials, 17)` | `(17,)` | input-only | `EEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_meg_rvq0..3` | reads `tok_meg` folder | `(128,)` each (one RVQ layer) | **output** (4 heads) | `MEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_eeg_out` | reads `tok_eeg` folder | `(17,)` | **output** (1 head) | `EEG_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_rgb` | `(196,)` int16 | `(196,)` | input + target | `TOK_RGB_VOCAB_SIZE` |
| `tok_depth` | `(196,)` int16 | `(196,)` | input + target | `TOK_DEPTH_VOCAB_SIZE` |

As **inputs**, MEG keeps its `16×8` spatiotemporal grid (4 RVQ layers summed inside
`MegEncoderEmbedding`); `tok_meg` / `tok_eeg` are encoded but never predicted. As
**outputs** (a reconstruction regularizer, e.g. `configs/4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml`),
MEG is predicted by 4 parallel heads — one per RVQ layer (`tok_meg_rvq0..3`,
`type: neural_grid`) — and EEG by one head (`tok_eeg_out`). The output heads read the same
on-disk folders (no repack); the loader picks one trial per sample and splits it so the 4
MEG heads stay coherent, and they are kept **out of the validation tasks** by design. Why
each axis/role is treated this way + the trial↔loss coherence guarantee:
[`notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md`](../notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md) §6.

Assistant2026-05-27T20:56:49.315Z

Done. MEG and EEG are now trainable output modalities that act as a reconstruction regularizer, with no external/ml-4m/ edits and no changes to your validation tasks.

What I added

New decoder heads (fourm_neural_embeddings.py): - MegRVQDecoderEmbedding — 4 of these (one per RVQ layer), each a 128-cell 16×8 grid head over vocab 512, with the same axial positions (learned source ⊕ sincos time) as the encoder. - EegDecoderEmbedding — one head, 17 tokens, vocab 8192, sincos positions.

Registration (fourm_neural_modalities.py): tok_meg_rvq0..3 and tok_eeg_out, all type: neural_grid, reading the existing tok_meg/tok_eeg folders (no repack). The original input-only tok_meg/tok_eeg are untouched.

Coherent trial split (neural_trial_transform.py NeuralTargetSplitter, wired in fourm_dataloader.py): one trial sampled per sample, sliced into the 4 MEG heads so they describe the same token.

Masking + config (neural_masking.py, config_validate.py) route neural_grid through the parallel path and allow the heads as targets, plus a leak-free training config 4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml (in: rgb+depth → out: rgb+depth+meg_rvq*+eeg_out).

The three system-level decisions (the "why")

  1. Custom type: neural_grid, not img or seq_token. seq_token would route targets through 4M's autoregressive path that silently drops scattered targets (the "MEG loss = 0" bug). img would route correctly but the trainer forces max_tokens to a perfect square — and our grids are 128 and 17. A new type gets the parallel decoder and keeps the non-square max_tokens.
  2. 4 modalities = 4 heads. 4M computes one cross-entropy per modality; MEG's 4 layer-specific RVQ codebooks therefore need 4 modalities, exactly the §6 "4 logit heads" prescription — achieved without patching the loss.
  3. Predict neural from vision (output-only). Since MEG's input (tok_meg) and outputs (tok_meg_rvq*) are different modality names, having both leaks the answer; predicting from vision keeps the regularizer honest.

Your coherence question is now answered structurally and documented in notes/4m_neural_modality_design.md §6: the trial is sampled once in the loader, and that one tensor is both embedded and used as the loss target (d['ids'] = d['tensor']), so forward and backprop can't desync — and the shared split keeps the 4 heads on the same trial.

Tests (TDD, all green)

23 new tests across test_neural_output_modalities.py + a real-WDS-pipeline coherence test in test_4m_loader_integration.py: decoder-embedding contracts, registration, neural_grid masking, coherent split, config validation, and an integration test proving each head's loss is finite, receives gradient, and descends on an overfit batch. Suite: 219 passed.

One thing to flag (not mine)

tests/test_validate_4m.py currently fails to import — your working copy edited it to from validate_4m import _resolve_checkpoint, but that function isn't in validate_4m.py yet. Want me to add _resolve_checkpoint (looks like checkpoint-path resolution for the validator), or is that mid-edit on your end?

Tool reply2026-05-27T20:58:57.354Z
=== modal_smoke_train.py ===
"""Modal GPU smoke tests using production-style *_main.yaml + *_data.yaml configs.

From repo root::

    modal run 4m_training/modal_smoke_train.py --case prod_things
    modal run 4m_training/modal_smoke_train.py --case all

Fast checks without GPU train (no image rebuild on code edits)::

    modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun --config 4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_data.yaml
    modal run 4m_training/modal_smoke_train.py --case probe
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import os
import subprocess
import sys
import time
from pathlib import Path

import importlib.util
import modal

def _load_modal_image():
    for path in (
        __import__("pathlib").Path("/opt/repo/4m_training/modal/_modal_load.py"),
        __import__("pathlib").Path(__file__).resolve().parent / "_modal_load.py",
    ):
        if not path.is_file():
            continue
        spec = importlib.util.spec_from_file_location("_modal_load", path)
        loader = importlib.util.module_from_spec(spec)
        spec.loader.exec_module(loader)
        return loader.load_modal_image()
    raise ImportError("_modal_load.py not found (expected /opt/repo/4m_training on Modal)")


_mi = _load_modal_image()
REPO = _mi.REPO
ensure_fourm = _mi.ensure_fourm
train_image = _mi.train_image
training_env = _mi.training_env

app = modal.App("train-4m-smoke")
project_volume = modal.Volume.from_name(_mi.PROJECT_VOLUME_NAME)
PROJECT = _mi.PROJECT_MOUNT

SMOKE_CASES: dict[str, tuple[str, list[str]]] = {
    "prod_things": ("4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_main.yaml", []),
    "loss_decreases": ("4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_loss_main.yaml", []),
    "prod_things_neural_in": (
        "4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_main.yaml",
        ["--data_config", "4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_things_neural_in_data.yaml"],
    ),
    "prod_cc12m": ("4m_training/configs/4m_smoke_cc12m_main.yaml", []),
}


def _run_train(main_config_rel: str, extra_argv: list[str]) -> None:
    ensure_fourm()
    cfg = os.path.join(REPO, main_config_rel)
    cmd = [
        sys.executable,
        os.path.join(REPO, "4m_training/train_4m.py"),
        "train",
        "--config",
        cfg,
    ]
    if extra_argv:
        cmd.extend(["--", *extra_argv])
    env = {**training_env(), "CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES": "0"}
    print("running:", " ".join(cmd), flush=True)
    subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, cwd=REPO, env=env)


@app.function(image=train_image, volumes={PROJECT: project_volume}, timeout=60 * 10)
def probe_volume() -> None:
    """CPU path check on the project volume."""
    for base in (
        f"{PROJECT}/data/train/things/tok_rgb",
        f"{PROJECT}/data/train/cc12m/crop_settings",
        f"{PROJECT}/data/train/cc12m/tok_rgb@224",
    ):
        print(f"exists {base}:", os.path.isdir(base), flush=True)
        if os.path.isdir(base):
            tars = sorted(f for f in os.listdir(base) if f.endswith(".tar"))[:3]
            print(f"  sample tars: {tars}", flush=True)


@app.function(
    image=train_image,
    volumes={PROJECT: project_volume},
    gpu="T4",
    timeout=60 * 15,
    memory=32 * 1024,
)
def smoke_one(case: str) -> str:
    if case not in SMOKE_CASES:
        raise ValueError(f"unknown case {case!r}; choose from {list(SMOKE_CASES)}")
    main_cfg, extra = SMOKE_CASES[case]
    t0 = time.time()
    _run_train(main_cfg, extra)
    msg = f"OK {case} in {time.time() - t0:.1f}s"
    print(msg, flush=True)
    return msg


@app.local_entrypoint()
def main(case: str = "all") -> None:
    if case == "probe":
        probe_volume.remote()
        return
    if case == "all":
        print("\n".join(smoke_one.remote(name) for name in SMOKE_CASES))
    else:
        print(smoke_one.remote(case))

Tool reply2026-05-27T21:01:05.390Z
"""Shared Modal image for 4M training.

This file defines the container environment used by all modal_*.py scripts.
Edit this once when you change deps or paths — copy modal_train.py for new jobs.

Rebuild triggers (slow):
  - Changing pip/apt packages below
  - Changing Python version

Does NOT rebuild when you edit repo code (configs, train_4m.py, etc.):
  - Repo is mounted at container start via ``add_local_dir`` (no ``copy=True``)
  - ``fourm`` is installed editable once per container at runtime, not in the image
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import os
import subprocess
import sys
from pathlib import Path

import modal

# Where your repo appears inside the Modal container.
REPO = "/opt/repo"

# This file is at <repo>/4m_training/modal/modal_image.py.
_MODAL_DIR = Path(__file__).resolve().parent
_TRAINING_DIR = _MODAL_DIR.parent            # 4m_training
_REPO_ROOT = _TRAINING_DIR.parent            # repo root (mounted into the container)

# Single source of truth for paths: lib/repo_paths.py (edit there, not here).
sys.path.insert(0, str(_TRAINING_DIR / "lib"))
import repo_paths  # noqa: E402

PROJECT_VOLUME_NAME = repo_paths.PROJECT_VOLUME_NAME   # your Modal volume name
PROJECT_MOUNT = "/project"                             # mount path is fixed

# Step 1: build a base image with system + Python packages.
# Changing anything here triggers a slow image rebuild.
# Stick to Python 3.10 — stock 4M breaks on 3.11+ (random.sample on dict views).
_deps_image = (
    modal.Image.debian_slim(python_version="3.10")
    .apt_install("git", "libgl1", "libglib2.0-0")
    .pip_install(
        "numpy<2",
        "torch",
        "torchvision",
        "webdataset",
        "pyyaml",
        "tokenizers",
        "einops",
        "timm",
        "opencv-python-headless",
    )
)

# Your local 4M checkout — taken from repo_paths (set ML4M_DIR_OVERRIDE there).
ML4M_LOCAL = repo_paths.ML4M_DIR

# Where 4M lands in the container, and whether it needs its own mount.
try:
    _rel = ML4M_LOCAL.relative_to(_REPO_ROOT)        # 4M lives inside the repo (default)
    ML4M_CONTAINER = f"{REPO}/{_rel.as_posix()}"
    _ml4m_outside_repo = False
except ValueError:                                   # 4M is elsewhere — mount it separately
    ML4M_CONTAINER = "/opt/ml-4m"
    _ml4m_outside_repo = True

# Step 2: attach your local repo to the container at /opt/repo.
# Syncs at container start — code edits on your machine show up without rebuilding.
train_image = _deps_image.add_local_dir(str(_REPO_ROOT), remote_path=REPO)
if _ml4m_outside_repo:
    train_image = train_image.add_local_dir(str(ML4M_LOCAL), remote_path=ML4M_CONTAINER)

# Marker file so we only pip-install fourm once per container.
_FOURM_READY = "/tmp/.fourm_editable_ok"


def ensure_fourm() -> None:
    """Make the 4M package importable inside the container."""
    if os.path.isfile(_FOURM_READY):
        return  # already installed on this container
    # Editable install from wherever 4M was mounted (inside the repo, or its own mount).
    subprocess.run(
        [sys.executable, "-m", "pip", "install", "-q", "-e", ML4M_CONTAINER],
        check=True,
    )
    Path(_FOURM_READY).write_text("ok\n")


def training_env() -> dict[str, str]:
    """Environment variables passed to the training subprocess."""
    return {
        **os.environ,
        # So Python finds our library modules (4m_training/lib) and upstream 4M.
        "PYTHONPATH": f"{REPO}/4m_training/lib:{ML4M_CONTAINER}",
        # Tell the in-container subprocess (repo_paths) where 4M is.
        "FOURM_ML4M_DIR": ML4M_CONTAINER,
        # 4M always uses DDP; these fake a single-GPU run.
        "RANK": "0",
        "WORLD_SIZE": "1",
        "LOCAL_RANK": "0",
        "MASTER_ADDR": "127.0.0.1",
        "MASTER_PORT": "29500",
    }

2	
3	This is a thin launcher: it starts a Modal container and runs train_4m.py inside it.
4	Shared setup (deps, repo mount, pip install 4M) lives in modal_image.py.
5	
6	Run from repo root::
7	
8	    modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --config 4m_training/configs/4m_things_main.yaml
9	
10	Dryrun on the volume (no GPU, no training — fast config/data check)::
11	
12	    modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun --config 4m_training/configs/4m_things_data.yaml
13	
14	Image rebuilds only when ``modal_image.py`` pip/apt deps change, not when you edit YAML or Python.
15	"""
16	
17	from __future__ import annotations
18	
19	import os
20	import subprocess
21	import sys
22	from pathlib import Path
23	
24	import importlib.util
25	import modal
26	
27	
28	def _load_modal_image():
29	    """Load shared image config — works locally and inside Modal containers."""
30	    for path in (
31	        __import__("pathlib").Path("/opt/repo/4m_training/modal/_modal_load.py"),
32	        __import__("pathlib").Path(__file__).resolve().parent / "_modal_load.py",
33	    ):
34	        if not path.is_file():
35	            continue
36	        spec = importlib.util.spec_from_file_location("_modal_load", path)
37	        loader = importlib.util.module_from_spec(spec)
38	        spec.loader.exec_module(loader)
39	        return loader.load_modal_image()
40	    raise ImportError("_modal_load.py not found (expected /opt/repo/4m_training on Modal)")
41	
42	
43	# Pull shared settings from modal_image.py (paths, image, env, ensure_fourm).
44	_mi = _load_modal_image()
45	REPO = _mi.REPO
46	ensure_fourm = _mi.ensure_fourm
47	train_image = _mi.train_image
48	training_env = _mi.training_env
49	
50	# Modal app name (shows up in the Modal dashboard).
51	app = modal.App("train-4m-things")
52	
53	# Persistent storage for data shards and checkpoints (name configurable in modal_image.py).
54	project_volume = modal.Volume.from_name(_mi.PROJECT_VOLUME_NAME)
55	PROJECT = _mi.PROJECT_MOUNT
56	
57	
58	def _run_train(config: str, dryrun: bool, n_batches: int) -> None:
59	    """Install 4M if needed, then run train_4m.py as a subprocess."""
60	    ensure_fourm()
61	
62	    # Config paths in YAML are relative to repo root.
63	    cfg = config
64	    if not os.path.isabs(cfg):
65	        cfg = os.path.join(REPO, cfg)
66	
67	    # This is the actual command that runs inside the container.
68	    cmd = [
69	        sys.executable,
70	        os.path.join(REPO, "4m_training/train_4m.py"),
71	        "dryrun" if dryrun else "train",
72	        "--config",
73	        cfg,
74	    ]
75	    if dryrun:
76	        cmd.extend(["--n-batches", str(n_batches)])
77	
78	    env = training_env()
79	    print("running:", " ".join(cmd), flush=True)
80	    subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, cwd=REPO, env=env)
81	
82	
83	@app.function(
84	    image=train_image,
85	    volumes={PROJECT: project_volume},  # mount volume at /project
86	    gpu="A100",
87	    timeout=60 * 60 * 24,
88	    memory=64 * 1024,
89	)
90	def train(config: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_main.yaml") -> None:
91	    """Full GPU training job."""
92	    _run_train(config, dryrun=False, n_batches=4)
93	
94	
95	@app.function(
96	    image=train_image,
97	    volumes={PROJECT: project_volume},
98	    timeout=60 * 30,
99	    memory=32 * 1024,
100	    # No gpu= — runs on CPU only (cheaper sanity check).
101	)
102	def dryrun_job(
103	    config: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_data.yaml",
104	    n_batches: int = 4,
105	) -> None:
106	    """CPU-only dataloader smoke test — use this before paying for GPU train."""
107	    _run_train(config, dryrun=True, n_batches=n_batches)
108	
109	
110	@app.function(
111	    image=train_image,
112	    volumes={PROJECT: project_volume},
113	    gpu="T4",
114	    timeout=60 * 60,
115	    memory=32 * 1024,
116	)
117	def validate_job(
118	    config: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_main.yaml",
119	    tasks: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_val_tasks.yaml",
120	    select: str = "",
121	    checkpoint: str = "",
122	    n_batches: int = 0,
123	) -> None:
124	    """Run named validation tasks on the project volume (optionally from a checkpoint)."""
125	    ensure_fourm()
126	    cmd = [
127	        sys.executable, os.path.join(REPO, "4m_training/validate_4m.py"),
128	        "--config", os.path.join(REPO, config),

130	        "--n-batches", str(n_batches),
131	    ]
132	    if select:

134	    if checkpoint:
135	        cmd += ["--checkpoint", checkpoint]
136	    print("running:", " ".join(cmd), flush=True)
137	    subprocess.run(cmd, check=True, cwd=REPO, env=training_env())
138	
139	
140	@app.local_entrypoint()
141	def main(
142	    config: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_main.yaml",
143	    dryrun: bool = False,
144	    validate: bool = False,
145	    tasks: str = "4m_training/configs/4m_things_val_tasks.yaml",
146	    select: str = "",
147	    checkpoint: str = "",
148	    n_batches: int = 4,
149	) -> None:
150	    """Called by `modal run` on your laptop — dispatches to a remote Modal function.
151	
152	    Examples::
153	        modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --dryrun --config .../4m_things_data.yaml
154	        modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --validate --select rgb2depth,anyany_neural
155	        modal run 4m_training/modal_train.py --validate --checkpoint /project/runs/.../checkpoint-last.pth
156	    """
157	    # Flags must not be named after a Modal function (e.g. `dryrun_job`/`validate_job`).
158	    if validate:
159	        validate_job.remote(config=config, tasks=tasks, select=select,
160	                            checkpoint=checkpoint, n_batches=n_batches)
161	    elif dryrun:

Assistant2026-05-27T21:14:20.364Z

Found the real bug — and it's the same lib/ move biting again. The inner error:

lib/train_4m.py:289  text_tokenizer = Tokenizer.from_file(tok_path)
Exception: No such file or directory (os error 2)

train_4m.py computes _REPO_ROOT = _HERE.parent, which was correct when the file sat at 4m_training/train_4m.py — but now that it's in lib/, _HERE.parent is 4m_training/, not the repo root. So every _REPO_ROOT-relative path (text tokenizer, external/ml-4m, data configs) is off by one level. Let me confirm against repo_paths (the stated single source of truth) and fix it there.

input. EEG-as-both is leak-free (single modality split by `image_mask`), MEG-as-both is not.

### Training gotcha: `find_unused_params`

With many output heads (4 MEG + 1 EEG + vision) and a stochastic Dirichlet target budget,
some heads get **0 targets** on a given step, so their parameters produce no gradient.
Stock 4M wraps the model in DDP, which then raises *"Expected to have finished reduction…
parameters that were not used in producing loss"*. Pass `--find_unused_params` to
`run_training_4m.py` (or set `find_unused_params: true` in the main config) for any
neural-output run. Verified on Modal (`modal_smoke_train.py --case loss_decreases_neural_out`):
all five neural losses are finite at step 0 and the MEG heads descend over 8 epochs.

This was breaking all GPU training, not just neural.

Neural-output–specific requirement

With 7 heads and a stochastic target budget, some heads get 0 targets per step → their params are unused → DDP errors. The fix is --find_unused_params (baked into the smoke case; documented in notes §6 and the config). For your real neural-output training, set find_unused_params: true in the main config.

Assistant2026-05-27T21:51:52.266Z
Thinking
Assistant2026-05-27T21:52:08.067Z

Short answer: because neither tok_meg nor tok_eeg can be a working out_domain in their current form — one for a hard structural reason, the other for a design/safety reason. The new tok_meg_rvq0..3 / tok_eeg_out modalities exist precisely to be the targets that tok_meg/tok_eeg can't be.

tok_meg — structurally impossible as one target

4M computes one softmax head per modality (fm.py:597 — a single cross_entropy(logits, target_ids)). But one MEG cell after the trial pick is (128, 4): 128 grid cells, each carrying 4 RVQ codes from 4 layer-specific 512-vocab codebooks. A single head can't emit 4 codes per position, and you can't merge them into one 512-vocab head because code 5 in layer 0 ≠ code 5 in layer 3. So MEG needs 4 heads = 4 modalities (tok_meg_rvq0..3). That's exactly your own §6 prescription ("4 logit heads, one per RVQ layer"). Putting tok_meg in out_domains would also just crash model build — it has decoder_embedding: None.

tok_eeg — could be one head, but reusing the name is the wrong move

EEG is (17,), single codebook — so in principle tok_eeg itself could carry a head. I deliberately made a separate tok_eeg_out instead, for three reasons:

  1. No churn / additive. tok_eeg is registered type: seq_token with an encoder embedding only. To make the same name a target I'd have to change its type → neural_grid and bolt on a decoder head — which would alter the input-only behavior your anyany_neural val task and the H1/H5 invariant tests depend on. A new tok_eeg_out leaves all of that untouched.
  2. Leakage. If tok_eeg were in both in_domains and out_domains, the encoder would see EEG tokens the decoder is asked to predict (their masks are sampled independently, so they overlap) → the model copies the answer → ~0 gradient → useless regularizer. Predicting tok_eeg_out from vision keeps it honest.
  3. Symmetry. MEG is forced into separate _rvq* output modalities anyway, so keeping EEG's target as a separate tok_eeg_out makes "neural inputs" vs "neural output heads" a clean, uniform distinction.

And there's no data duplication: tok_meg_rvq* / tok_eeg_out set path: tok_meg / path: tok_eeg, so they read the same on-disk folders — they're just views that the loader splits per head.

So the validator's rule "tok_meg/tok_eeg may not be out_domains" (config_validate.py) is intentional, and the way you do train neural as output is to put tok_meg_rvq0-tok_meg_rvq1-tok_meg_rvq2-tok_meg_rvq3-tok_eeg_out in out_domains (as in 4m_smoke_things_neural_out_data.yaml).

Note you're looking at 4m_things_data.yaml — I left that one as input-only on purpose (it's your main/production data config and the README treats it as the input-only reference). Want me to add the neural output heads to 4m_things_data.yaml's out_domains too, or add a separate production *_neural_out_data.yaml alongside it so the input-only config stays intact?

Assistant2026-05-27T21:58:52.962Z
Thinking
Assistant2026-05-27T21:59:04.705Z

You're thinking about it almost exactly right — and you've put your finger on the one place my current build doesn't match that mental model. Let me confirm each point, then show the wrinkle.

Where you're right: 1. "Predict everything from everything" — yes, that's 4M's native any-to-any objective: every modality is partly input, partly target, split by random masking. Including neural means putting it in both in_domains and out_domains. 2. "One trial chosen, loss against that same trial" — exactly right, and it's the core coherence guarantee. My output heads already do this: the splitter picks one trial, and that same tensor is both embedded and used as the target ids (loss is against it). ✓ 3. "Sentinel → don't include MEG/EEG for that image" — already handled: meg_mask/eeg_mask = 0 zeroes both the input and target budget for that sample, so the placeholder never reaches the encoder or contributes loss. ✓

The wrinkle (and the gap in what I built). A normal modality (RGB, depth, EEG) has one code per cell, so masking cleanly splits its cells into "shown to the encoder" vs "predicted by the decoder" — your exact picture, one trial, leak-free. MEG breaks this: each of its 128 cells carries 4 RVQ codes, so it needs 4 prediction heads → it can't be a single modality the way RGB is.

That's why I built MEG's input (tok_meg, the summed grid) and output (tok_meg_rvq*) as separate modalities. And here's the real problem you intuited: today those separate modalities pick trials independently and are masked independently. So if I naively add MEG to both in_domains and out_domains, the encoder would see one trial while the decoder predicts another — violating your "same trial" rule — and the masks would overlap (encoder sees cells the decoder must predict → leak). My current code is only correct for the output-only case.

To honor your any-to-any vision properly, the clean fix is to stop summing on the input and instead treat each RVQ layer as its own normal modality — tok_meg_rvq0..3, each a single-code 128-cell grid, each in both in_domains and out_domains, all four sharing the one sampled trial. Then 4M's standard masking splits each layer's 128 cells into shown/predicted, leak-free, loss against that trial — exactly your model. EEG becomes a single tok_eeg that's both input and target (it's single-codebook, so it already works like RGB). This is a real rebuild of what I shipped (the output-only heads), so I want your call on it:

Assistant2026-05-27T21:59:13.337Z

{
  "questions": [
    {
